  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a7e1f51c-83ba-4d2a-9c6c-0062f304b962'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/523236-so-am-i-correct-in-stating-that-we-are"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So... Am I correct in stating that we are supposed to believe that Elara was not under Coriane's influence when she was singing to her? That Elara was able to escape her influence and lied, telling her she wasn't giving Coriane nightmares, leading Coriane deeper into her depression and paranoia? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think that was the point, but it just seemed a little convoluted. I know that Arven the silence or whatever was supposed to take care of her but had<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think that was the point, but it just seemed a little convoluted. I know that Arven the silence or whatever was supposed to take care of her but had he already sided with Elara? were they all in on it from then? It leave a lot open. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526985355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13403913129099676107"><blockquote>
<i><b>"There is nothing so terrible as a story untold."</b></i> </blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_' title='Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Queen Song</a> is one of the novellas of <b>Red Queen</b> series. Here, we are told about the backstory of <b>Queen Coriane</b>, the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b> from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a>. Coriane belongs to the Silver blood, under the <i>House Jacos</i>-- a not-so-well-endowed clan compared to other Silver bloods. She writes her life events in a dairy and conveys her emotions there. Her ordinary life changed when <b>Prince Tibe</b>, heir to the <i>court of Norta</i>, fell in love with her and asked he</span>
  <span id="freeText13403913129099676107" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<i><b>"There is nothing so terrible as a story untold."</b></i> </blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_" title="Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen Song</a> is one of the novellas of <b>Red Queen</b> series. Here, we are told about the backstory of <b>Queen Coriane</b>, the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>. Coriane belongs to the Silver blood, under the <i>House Jacos</i>-- a not-so-well-endowed clan compared to other Silver bloods. She writes her life events in a dairy and conveys her emotions there. Her ordinary life changed when <b>Prince Tibe</b>, heir to the <i>court of Norta</i>, fell in love with her and asked her hand for marriage, which of course, became the reason why the traditional <i>Queenstrial</i> was never realized. This led to conflicts and certain intrigues that tested Coriane's strength and belief while carrying her crown as a Queen.<br><br>It's Victoria Aveyard's flawless and breathtaking writing style that made me embrace this novella. Once again I was amazed by how she was able to bring this story in an epic level. There were no action scenes here but all the events were simply engaging. I loved how the simple plotline surprisingly became extraordinarily beautiful in the end.<br><br>The <b>romance</b> between Coriane and Tibe was sweet and raw, heartbreaking at times. There was also a good pacing here and the Silver blood's powers were drawn neatly.<br><br>Perhaps Coriane's <b>character development</b> was the one that's lacking here. She came out fragile and weak in the beginning but she was starting to get tough in the near-end. Unfortunately, she went back to being weak again in the end, surrendering to her fate and accepting her vulnerability that she couldn't do anything to save herself and the people she cared about.<br><br>All in all, this novella is totally compelling despite some minor flaws. It's nice to know Coriane's story after she was mysteriously mentioned in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>. It was written in a poignant yet beautiful prose, something that holds you together to read it. When it comes to the ending, it was a bit hazy and mind-boggling, thus leaving us with a big question: <b>WHO DID IT?</b><br><br>Rating:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445994440i/16731146.jpg" width="200" height="45" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445993261i/16730770.jpg" width="200" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13403913129099676107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2047872675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047872675" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047872675?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047872675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2304300600526706891">Okay first of all: <br/><br/>I always knew that Elara was an - excuse my crude choice of words - evil bitch, but holy mackerel that probably was the understatement of the century! That woman is pure evil and after reading “Queen Song” I just want that witch to burn. XD<br/><br/>Well, enough of the pleasantries and back to the review. Since it was just a short novella I decided to point out what I liked and what I didn’t like. That way you don’t have to put up with my endless babbling and ranting and still will have</span>
  <span id="freeText2304300600526706891" style="display:none">Okay first of all: <br /><br />I always knew that Elara was an - excuse my crude choice of words - evil bitch, but holy mackerel that probably was the understatement of the century! That woman is pure evil and after reading “Queen Song” I just want that witch to burn. XD<br /><br />Well, enough of the pleasantries and back to the review. Since it was just a short novella I decided to point out what I liked and what I didn’t like. That way you don’t have to put up with my endless babbling and ranting and still will have enough time to continue to read your (no doubt) awesome books! ;-)<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Warning: The review might contain some minor spoilers from now on!</b>
</u><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>What I didn’t like:</b>
</u><br /><br />-	It took a little while until the story line picked up pace and even though there were only six chapters the first 3 were pretty lengthy. <br />-	I wanted to read more about Julian and Sara but the two unfortunately were once again degraded to be side characters. So yeah, not much of additional info on that front.<br />-	After chapter three everything went to hell! *lol* Hmm okay, I’m not even sure if that’s negative so let’s just scratch this, okay? xD<br /><br /><u>
  <b>What I liked:</b>
</u><br /><br />-	I loved the gentle and balanced relationships between Prince Robert, King Tiberias Calore V. and Queen Anabel. Those three really seemed to care for each other and it was more than just nice to see how much they respected and loved each other. =D<br />-	I liked that Prince Tibe chose Coriane because he truly loved her and didn’t give a damn about Queenstrial. Haha<br />-	I loved how I was shaken after the last chapter. All those different feels… *shudder*<br />-	And in addition to that I enjoyed how intense the book became once Coriane moved to the court. Jeez! I’m still having heart palpitations here. *lol*<br />-	The way Coriane loved everything about her little baby boy Cal! XD<br /><br />So yeah even though the novella started kind of slow it really got to me in the end. What made it even worse were Coriane’s diary entries and her thoughts that actually caused me to swallow. Over those last two chapters the book got an oppressive edge and my heart literally skipped some beats. <br /><br />In conclusion as always a few quotes I liked:<br /><br /><i>“She walked the city many times in hopes of finding a place she enjoyed, somewhere to anchor her in the newly tossing sea of her life.<br />She found no such place – instead she found a person.”</i><br /><br /><i>“The boy was the sun in Coriane’s sky. On hard days, he split the darkness. On good days, he lit the world.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>*Super spoiler quotes!!! Don't click if you don't want to know the end*</u>
</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>“The only person in my head is me.<br />The only person who has not changed is you. You are still the little girl in a dusty room, forgotten, unwanted, out of place. You are queen of everything, mother to a beautiful son, wife to a king who loves you, and still you cannot find it in yourself to smile.<br />Still you make nothing.<br />Still you are empty.<br />The only person in your head is you.<br />And she is no one of any importance.<br />She is nothing.”</i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <i>“She destroyed the book like she destroyed Coriane.<br />And she dreamed of nothing.”</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If you liked the Red Queen series this is definitely a good addition to the books and certainly will help you to bridge the time until the fourth book finally arrives!!!</span>

<div id="review_2189418122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189418122" />
    <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis"><img alt="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585764390p2/6603759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189418122?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis">☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189418122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6723624213675047911">Not sure if I liked it. Though maybe I did. The beginning was a bit unpleasant but then it progressed into quite a neat introduction to a world. The Red Queen World. <br/><br/>The final accords - lovely and lively. A warrior queen. A king and his 'paramour', M-M style. A prince who 'intoxicates' himself. A girl who likes equations and mechanisms. A guy who loves history. Stuffy nobility, Silver and gifted. Reds, blesed with purpose to their lives.<br/><br/>And Coriane's final... what a crescendo!<br/><br/>Q:<br/>There is nothing </span>
  <span id="freeText6723624213675047911" style="display:none">Not sure if I liked it. Though maybe I did. The beginning was a bit unpleasant but then it progressed into quite a neat introduction to a world. The Red Queen World. <br /><br />The final accords - lovely and lively. A warrior queen. A king and his 'paramour', M-M style. A prince who 'intoxicates' himself. A girl who likes equations and mechanisms. A guy who loves history. Stuffy nobility, Silver and gifted. Reds, blesed with purpose to their lives.<br /><br />And Coriane's final... what a crescendo!<br /><br />Q:<br />There is nothing so terrible as a story untold. (c)<br />Q:<br />And her gray eyes, once bright stars, seemed dark, full of shadows. (c)<br />Q:<br />I remember. There is no greater pain or punishment than memory. (c)<br />Q:<br />They drank in the morning with greed, a quenched man still gulping at water while others died of thirst. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Always a plan with you.”<br />“I certainly try.” (c)<br />Q:<br />She was no great intellect, charmer, beauty, or warrior. Her usefulness lay in marriage, in alliance, and there were none to be found in her brother’s books or protection. (c)<br />Q:<br />Queen Anabel, an oblivion of House Lerolan, did just that. She sat on the king’s left, her smile curling, eyes on her only son. Her military uniform was open at the neck, revealing a firestorm of jewels at her throat, red and orange and yellow as the explosive ability she possessed. (c)<br />Q:<br />At least she has spine enough to eat her food. (c)<br />Q:<br />A strange prince, an even stranger night, she wrote later. I don’t know if I ever want to see him again. But he seemed lonely too. Should we not be lonely together? (c)<br />Q:<br />I leave behind unfinished puzzles, pieces never put back together. It feels wasteful. Not of the objects, but myself. So much time spent stripping wire or counting screws. For what? For knowledge I will never use? Knowledge that is cursed, inferior, stupid, to everyone else? What have I done with myself for fifteen years? A great construct of nothing. (c)<br />Q:<br />She walked the city many times in hopes of finding a place she enjoyed, somewhere to anchor her in the newly tossing sea of her life. (c)<br />Q:<br />Coriane was not so dazzled by silk shops or the stylish eateries jutting out over the water, but more interested in the bridge itself, its construction. She tried to fathom how many tons of metal were beneath her feet, her mind a flurry of equations. (c)<br />Q:<br />“I was just wondering how many tons of metal we’re standing on, hoping it will keep us up.”<br />... <br />“I’ll do my best to keep that thought out of my head,” he mumbled. “Any other frightening notions to share?” (c)<br />Q:<br />The cage of the capital was not a happy place for Coriane.<br />Nor Tiberias Calore. (c)<br />Q:<br />She thought that every time, and she was always wrong. (c)<br />Q:<br />How could servants create such beauty and still be considered inferior? They are capable of wonders different from our own. <br />They gained skill through handiwork and practice, rather than birth. Is that not equal to Silver strength, if not greater than it? But she did not dwell on such thoughts long. She never did. This is the way of the world. (c)<br />Q:<br />Something tightened in Coriane’s chest, an unfamiliar sensation. Was it . . . happiness? She thought so. (c)<br />Q:<br />We are the same, she thought. Searching for something to keep us anchored, both alone in a crowded room. (c)<br />Q:<br />But there is a difference between a single candle in darkness, and a sunrise. (c)<br />Q:<br />“It gets easier,” Queen Anabel whispered into her ear. Coriane wanted to believe her. (c)<br />Q:<br />Usually this is where the fairy tale ends. Stories don’t go much further than this moment, and I fear there’s a good reason for it. (c)<br />Q:<br />... simply could not believe how her mind seemed to spin out of control, happy one second and then distraught the next, bouncing between emotions like a kite in a gale. (c)<br />Q:<br />It might be a crime to write such things, but I am a queen. I am the queen. I can say and write what I think. (c)<br />Q:<br />You are still the little girl in a dusty room, forgotten, unwanted, out of place. You are queen of everything, mother to a beautiful son, wife to a king who loves you, and still you cannot find it in yourself to smile. (c)</span>

<div id="review_1215522954" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1215522954" />
    <a title="Fatima  Havilliard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36812736-fatima-havilliard"><img alt="Fatima  Havilliard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481594049p2/36812736.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fatima  Havilliard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fatima  Havilliard" href="/user/show/36812736-fatima-havilliard">Fatima  Havilliard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36812736-fatima-havilliard?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1215522954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12896416455448073368"><b>"The Calores are children of fire, as strong and destructive as their flame, but Cal will not be like the others before. Fire can destroy, fire can kill, but it can also create. Forest burned in the summer will be green by spring, better and stronger than before. Cal’s flame will build and bring roots from the ashes of war. The guns will quiet, the smoke will clear, and the soldiers, Red and Silver both, will come home. One hundred years of war, and my son will bring peace. He will not die fight</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12896416455448073368" style="display:none"><b>"The Calores are children of fire, as strong and destructive as their flame, but Cal will not be like the others before. Fire can destroy, fire can kill, but it can also create. Forest burned in the summer will be green by spring, better and stronger than before. Cal’s flame will build and bring roots from the ashes of war. The guns will quiet, the smoke will clear, and the soldiers, Red and Silver both, will come home. One hundred years of war, and my son will bring peace. He will not die fighting. He will not. HE WILL NOT."</b> <br /><br />I think I love Coriane. <br /><br />Queen Song is a novella about The deceased Queen Coriane, the mother of Cal. This confirm that Elara is a bitch in all the extension of the word!! And this pulled me out of some doubts, I really hope that in Glass Sword tell us more about House Jacos and the powers of the silvers. Also I love the words Coriane write in her diary about Cal and the love she had for him and her desire for that he will change the things when he reign. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[something that probably doesn't happen because of Maven Lol <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donita Luz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donita Luz" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz">Donita Luz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555999735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13878368135203624441"><blockquote>
  <i>"He was the prince. the future king. And she was no one at all, a limp excuse for a Silver daughter of a High House."</i>
</blockquote> This novella was clever. I have been so curious with the first queen, Cal's mother story. All we got to know her was that she was the king's first wife, a Singer, Julian's sister and the queen before the cold-hearted Elara took over. It was written on a third-person point of view given the fact that Queen Coriane has already past away - wasn't expecting that. I thought that t</span>
  <span id="freeText13878368135203624441" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"He was the prince. the future king. And she was no one at all, a limp excuse for a Silver daughter of a High House."</i>
</blockquote> This novella was clever. I have been so curious with the first queen, Cal's mother story. All we got to know her was that she was the king's first wife, a Singer, Julian's sister and the queen before the cold-hearted Elara took over. It was written on a third-person point of view given the fact that Queen Coriane has already past away - wasn't expecting that. I thought that this novella was going to be composed of entry on a Diary where the queen kept all of her secrets - I was obviously wrong and it was the best mistake ever.<br /><br />Queen Song was simply amazing. Coriane and Tibe's love story was also included and even though it was not really detailed I couldn't have asked for more. It was like a Cinderella story, only Coriane was not a slave, although they are poor, they still belong to a High House with a Silver Blood and instead of a wicked Step-mother, we got here instead a wicked/evil queen wanna be in Elara. Although tragic, it was sweet and believable, being a crowned prince and all. We also get to follow the Queen's happiness and hurt and anger and desperation and depression when she was finally able to get a son, Cal, after the 3rd miscarriage. <br /><br />Her characterization was well portrayed, although a bit unlikeable. She likes to down herself a lot even before she met the crowned prince, always moping around feeling sorry for herself, for the dream she wouldn't be able to live, she was weak. She did tried to fight, however, she didn't know her enemy well which eventually end up to her death as we all know.<br /><br />The ending was obviously rushed. I think it has something to do with the secrecy and mystery that the book is trying to keep up. Although we all have our suspicions, the question still remains on who really is behind the Queen's death? and.. How?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13878368135203624441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6784352887011409201" style="display:none">It is always fun when author's give us this look inside a character, whether they be good or evil but I must admit, its the evil ones, that really stand out and get my attention.<br /><br />To be inside their heads, even from a distance as is the case in this story, just fascinates me and really does add depth to the character. <br /><br />I feel for Cal and for the woman that he would never get to love or know and of course for the woman that dared to cross Elara's path.<br /><br />I absolutely love that the author gave us this. I thoroughly enjoyed it and thought it was a great addition to the series. To see how it all started, how it all came about, was a treat and I can't wait to dive into book two now. </span>

  5 out of 10
</b><br /><br /><a href="http://www.livelib.ru/review/549661" rel="nofollow noopener">ревью на русском/review in russian</a><br /><br />The start was really confusing: it seemed like the language wasn't English at all - very hard to read and enjoy. But on the chapter #2 I had recognized Victoria's old style, it was a relief. The story itself is indeed sad, we all know that Coriane will be dead and Elara will take her place. At the start I thought that Cal's mother was a brat and angsty chick, but I loved her later. It was interesting to see young Tiberias the Sixth and his parents, but I was happier when Cal was born. Such a shame this story wasn't about this fat and cute baby) Overall, the bonus is nice (not super necessary but totally not a waste of time). <br /><br /><b>Red Queen (Алая королева):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219807950" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen Song (Песнь королевы)</a> #0.1/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312174580" rel="nofollow noopener">Steel Scars (Стальные шрамы)</a> #0.2/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268481" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469225994" rel="nofollow noopener">Алая Королева</a>) #1/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268493" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword (Стеклянный меч</a>) #2/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268496" rel="nofollow noopener">King's Cage (Королевская клетка)</a> #3/4<br />— Untitled (Без названия) #4/4</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_1532178412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532178412" />
    <a title="Nur Raihan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33582520-nur-raihan"><img alt="Nur Raihan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480086712p2/33582520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1532178412?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nur Raihan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nur Raihan" href="/user/show/33582520-nur-raihan">Nur Raihan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532178412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14798312635306692047">This novella is based on the <b>Red Queen</b> series and in this book, we are told about Queen Coriane. To those who have read Red Queen, <b>Queen Coriane</b> is the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b>. She's a Silver blood and came from <i>House Jacos</i>, a not really famous clan compared to the other Silver bloods. Every emotion and thought of hers are portrayed in a diary that was given by Julian for her birthday. Everything changes in her life when the <i>heir to the court of Norta</i>, <b>Prince Tribe</b> fell in love with her and asked h</span>
  <span id="freeText14798312635306692047" style="display:none">This novella is based on the <b>Red Queen</b> series and in this book, we are told about Queen Coriane. To those who have read Red Queen, <b>Queen Coriane</b> is the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b>. She's a Silver blood and came from <i>House Jacos</i>, a not really famous clan compared to the other Silver bloods. Every emotion and thought of hers are portrayed in a diary that was given by Julian for her birthday. Everything changes in her life when the <i>heir to the court of Norta</i>, <b>Prince Tribe</b> fell in love with her and asked her hand for marriage. This lead to conflicts that really tested her while being a Queen. <br /><br />I loved how this short story grabbed my attention even though it was short. I pity Queen Coriane how she had trouble with her carriage and she got pregnant for the <i>fourth time</i> at the age of 21 and finally had a baby, who turns out to be the precious <i>Prince Cal</i>. (It was funny how I'll be turning 21 soon but I'm still not married and this lady here just had her first child)<br /><br />Lol anyway, that wasn't my point. Queen Coriane started off as a weak character who was easily shaken off, especially by Elara (yes, that bitch) and she grew stronger from time to time, and then went straight back to being weak again? <b> AND THAT ENDING</b>. I'm not sure what happened. It was so abrupt! Like, why would you end it like that? I mean, who did that? But whatever it is, I'm glad that Prince Cal survived :)<br /><br /><i>Definitely recommending this to those who enjoyed Red Queen and are interested to know the backstory of Prince Cal's mother, Queen Coriane.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14798312635306692047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1469477870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469477870" />
    <a title="Lucy Qhuay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7115693-lucy-qhuay"><img alt="Lucy Qhuay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564407818p2/7115693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469477870?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Qhuay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Qhuay" href="/user/show/7115693-lucy-qhuay">Lucy Qhuay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=ultimate-favourites">ultimate-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=boulevard-of-broken-dreams">boulevard-of-broken-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=my-poor-heart">my-poor-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=extras-short-stories-novellas">extras-short-stories-novellas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469477870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer769961757475576247"><br/>Such a heartbreaking novella.<br/><br/>You know, Julian was right. I can definitely see Mare in Coriane. Mare is a more bitter, hardened version of the Singer Queen, but they have an astoundingly similar way of thinking.<br/><br/>Both stand alone in a sea of people, never sure of anything, least of all their place in the world, Strong in their own way too.<br/><br/>I could also see Cal in Coriane's love for building things and taking them apart to see how they function and that might have been the only thing that made me smi</span>
  <span id="freeText769961757475576247" style="display:none"><br />Such a heartbreaking novella.<br /><br />You know, Julian was right. I can definitely see Mare in Coriane. Mare is a more bitter, hardened version of the Singer Queen, but they have an astoundingly similar way of thinking.<br /><br />Both stand alone in a sea of people, never sure of anything, least of all their place in the world, Strong in their own way too.<br /><br />I could also see Cal in Coriane's love for building things and taking them apart to see how they function and that might have been the only thing that made me smile.<br /><br />Mother and son sure would have had a blast together. They would have created magnificent things.<br /><br />It wasn't fair. Elara was a vicious, heartless bitch. I can't believe how she wormed her way into Coriane's mind and slowly, but steadily led her to madness and death.<br /><br />Urrgh! I wanted her to go through all the terror she inflicted on Cal's mother. A thousand times worse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="769961757475576247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18140106798608296774">This was an okay novella. I didn't really understand anyone's part or what their roles might be in the novel. I think I might have enjoyed it more had I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a> first, but if/when I do read that one I'll probably reread this to see if it makes a difference. I did feel badly for Coriane and what she went through while being queen. The ending was quite good, which is probably the reason I gave it three stars.</span>

I did feel badly for Coriane and what she went through while being queen. The ending was quite good, which is probably the reason I gave it three stars.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian Chen (Vivian&#39;s Book Pavilion)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian Chen (Vivian&#39;s Book Pavilion)" href="/user/show/44480454-vivian-chen-vivian-s-book-pavilion">Vivian Chen (Vivian&#39;s Book Pavilion)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615587687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1474241673364936351">This is post originally on <a> Vivian's Book Pavilion </a><br/><br/><br/> I really like the old queen!!! And I think that everyone will like her as well, even the red. And, to my astonishment…the king and queen before Coriane and Tiberias seemed great as well!!!! It’s really sad that what happened to all of them, especially Coriane. She’s such a lonely girl when she was a child!!! And when she finally found her love? She was too afraid to embrace it, fortunately, she did, eventually. Or we won’t have Cal now.<br/><b>
  <i>
    </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText1474241673364936351" style="display:none">This is post originally on <a> Vivian's Book Pavilion </a><br /><br /><br /> I really like the old queen!!! And I think that everyone will like her as well, even the red. And, to my astonishment…the king and queen before Coriane and Tiberias seemed great as well!!!! It’s really sad that what happened to all of them, especially Coriane. She’s such a lonely girl when she was a child!!! And when she finally found her love? She was too afraid to embrace it, fortunately, she did, eventually. Or we won’t have Cal now.<br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> He needs someone strong at his side, a person who laughs at the gossips and overcome her own doubts.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /> How to say…? Coriane is extremely without confidence, really? Stand up for yourself!!!! But she is a good person, a good queen, and I think the “red &amp; silver” won’t happen on her. The only problem I have with this story is that Coriane and Tiberias sacrifice his children’s future marriage for themselves. Well…actually, Coriane objected, but Tiberias accepted to be with her. So? I really don’t know whether I should hate the decision or not, after all…like I said, without Coriane, without Cal. But I do like her story, especially with someone behind her, all the time. And, it gives us some positive insight into the palace, especially the old king and queen and Robert. They’re quit a character, and I like them! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1474241673364936351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eNFfsJPdLYpLXpLKL0PFNodB7SlaGgFtUSswwtdLIr3/HW8cvkgWFQfSo3JtICWVYDpYbYSSWJ7W+qTJWfkmhg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('T9W4G1SXVFsElphPUFlzDSAUa/a6xNv1yW7pEvg+k9vIGYi3eQJvxEgaqfcSOpOux2/esmRMggZOv30ZdoyX4A==')})
  }
